The Effect of Opium on the Brain and Spinal Cord 204

— Dr. She Lei

The effect of opium on the brain is similar in all vertebrates, but the degree of brain development varies, so the symptoms presented are also different.

According to animal experiments, when morphine is given to frogs, the function of the cerebrum disappears first, followed by the midbrain, then the cerebellum, and finally the function of the medulla oblongata disappears in succession. In higher animals, including humans, when morphine or opium is taken to a considerable tolerance level, the sensitivity of the cerebral cortex to strong sensory stimuli is dulled first. Therefore, it can reduce or even forget feelings of pain, fatigue, hunger, and suffering. The sensitivity of the respiratory center to stimuli is also reduced, so it can make coughing disappear. Consciousness is not reduced, so sleep does not occur. But later, these parts are also gradually affected, and the sensitivity to external stimuli gradually becomes dull and sleep occurs. At this time, all unpleasant feelings are forgotten, and the mind is in a trance, as if traveling in a dreamland. It feels a kind of indescribable pleasure. Those who abuse morphine or opium as an addiction probably have this effect, which is one of the reasons why people become addicted.

Any part of the brain is excited by opium or morphine. Sometimes irregular concepts arise, and the mental state changes rapidly, presenting a state of exaltation. It was previously thought that this was the excitatory effect of morphine or opium, but it is not actually excitation. This is because the various functions of the brain lose their balance, the conceptual realm has not been affected, and the sensitivity of sensation has decreased. External stimuli have very little influence, so only the conceptual realm dominates and irregular concepts arise, presenting a kind of excitatory state. Therefore, this situation is actually the early stage of anesthesia.

Amateur Ramblings

Small Newspaper Year 205

In the past few years, the small newspapers in Shanghai, and even the supplements of various major newspapers, could almost be said to be dressed in the colorful clothes of the Mandarin Ducks and Butterflies School. The anecdotes of Rogue Scholars, the tales of courtesans, the photos of famous actors and actresses, as well as essays and serial novels about women, were their main content. Readers could be found on trams, in shops, in amusement parks, and in teahouses. However, as the times trended "new," the Mandarin Ducks and Butterflies School gradually lost ground. First, the supplements of some major newspapers changed direction, and new literary works, miscellaneous essays, and notes replaced the masterpieces of the Shanghai School of writers and novelists. Recently, there have been even greater changes in the small newspaper world. The appearance of several newly published small newspapers is completely different from that of the original small newspapers. Their content includes current affairs commentary, academic lectures, science essays, social commentary, life sketches, news from various places, etc., almost like new small magazines. The so-called magazine-style small newspaper can truly be said to be their characteristic. At the same time, it is said that even among the most famous of the existing small newspapers, the number of copies sold is gradually decreasing, while the sales of several newly published small newspapers that have appeared with a new look are not bad. It is really hard to say whether this development will cause those old small newspapers to change direction. Thus, some people who are aware of the times say, "This year is the year of the small newspaper!" Indeed, it can be said that this year is the "year of the small newspaper," but what is the significance of this "year of the small newspaper"? How did it come about? People have not yet correctly answered this question.

A certain writer said that the progression from "something year" to "magazine year" and then from "magazine year" to "small newspaper year" indicates that China is regressing from "big" to "small," and that the Chinese people are good at "avoiding difficulties and taking the easy way," engaging in speculation and opportunism. From this, he concluded that "the Chinese nation has no hope." But I say this is a kind of formalism! Our solution to problems cannot be based solely on the form of the problem. Recently, a large number of ancient books have been printed by some bookstores, such as the Twenty-Six Histories, various "wenku" (collections of ancient Chinese books), and rare editions. Their form is very large, but we cannot say that they have the meaning of progress just because they are "big." Similarly, we cannot say that small newspapers appearing in a new form are a sign of regression just because they are "small." The evaluation should mainly come from their content. In fact, the newly published so-called magazine-style small newspapers are naturally not as "big" as those large magazines in terms of form, but judging from their content, they are at least much more advanced than those small newspapers that used to be dressed in the colorful clothes of the Mandarin Ducks and Butterflies School. Therefore, we believe that the appearance of the "year of the small newspaper" is not a symbol of China's regression, and even less can it be said that "the Chinese nation has no hope." Rather, it has a certain progressive significance.

As for the reason for the appearance of the "year of the small newspaper," it is certainly not due to the "speculation and opportunism" of those who founded the new small newspapers, but rather has its social basis. Here, we can put forward several points:

First, we believe that although Chinese culture is generally relatively backward, the speed of ideological progress in China in recent years has been very fast. From the May Fourth Movement through the May Thirtieth Movement to the present, although it has only been a little over ten years, the ideological progress of China has almost gone through the centuries that Western Europe has gone through in the past. This is an undeniable historical fact. Under such ideological progress, publications that talk about women and promote low-level interests have been abandoned by most people who live seriously. Humorous articles that once made some people feel happy have also become overly pedantic. What is now popular is popular academic writing and science essays. The so-called "year of the small newspaper" has emerged under this influence.

Secondly, the readers of small newspapers are mainly small and medium-sized merchants, shop assistants, apprentices, some workers, and unemployed and out-of-school youth. In this era of economic panic and depressing life, along with the progress of social thought, the desire to seek knowledge

Page 20

The desire to seek knowledge is also growing day by day. Even if they spend two or three copper coins to buy a small newspaper, they have to think about it. Among many small newspapers, they must buy the one that can give them the most useful knowledge. Those things that talk about low-level interests are certainly not what they need at present. Therefore, some people have seized the opportunity to start some new small newspapers, and that is how the "year of the small newspaper" came about.

Finally, the so-called economic downturn is also fundamentally related to the appearance of the "year of the small newspaper." Because of the downturn in industry and commerce and the reduction in general purchasing power, even to start a small business requires a lot of capital. As for large social undertakings, they require even more substantial capital to carry out. This is also the case in the cultural world. If you want to take out tens of thousands of dollars to start a large newspaper or a large bookstore or even a large magazine, it is unlikely that you will be able to run it well and maintain it for a long time. On the other hand, if you use the money for running a large newspaper to run a small newspaper, or use the money for running a bookstore or a large magazine to run a small weekly, as long as you can recognize the needs of the readers and manage it well, you will have a good future. The current era is an era of using big money to run small businesses. Therefore, some smart people have raised relatively large amounts of capital to run small newspapers. In fact, don't the several new small newspapers that have recently appeared have capital of 100,000 to 80,000 yuan?

The advancement of social thought, the general readers' rejection of low-level interests, and the demand for useful and progressive knowledge: these are the objective requirements for the emergence of new small newspapers. The economic downturn in industry and commerce, and the reliability of only using big money to run small businesses: these are the economic conditions for the emergence of new small newspapers. The general reason for the emergence of the "year of the small newspaper" lies here.

As for the quality of the several small newspapers that have recently appeared in a new form, we do not want to make arbitrary judgments here. We only say that they must have content and form that are suitable for the needs of the general readers in order to have a great future. If a new small newspaper can use high-quality paper and a very scientific printing technique to print very substantial content, and sell it at a very low price, then I dare say that it will be warmly welcomed and supported by everyone and will develop rapidly. On the other hand, if it only boasts in advertisements, only improves the form of the newspaper, and only uses a few unqualified "celebrities" to appeal, while the content is full of outdated ideas and even still promotes low-level interests, then I dare say that it will be increasingly despised and will move towards its own death. The current era is different. Even the readers of small newspapers want to see good goods. Advertisements and "celebrities" can only play a role under good goods!

Celebrity Interview

King of Football, Li Huitang 206

— Prisoner of the Past

Li Huitang lives in a very luxurious apartment along Xizhe Road. It is a nine-story giant building, shooting straight into the sky like a pen tube. Outside the gate is a circular lawn, which looks a bit like a spittoon next to such a giant building. I walked along the car lane on the edge of the lawn for about several tens of steps and arrived at a vast and magnificent living room. After taking the name card in, a young man with a long figure wearing a blue-gray suit came out of the elevator, greeted me to sit down, and after a few "idle words" between each other, we "got down to business."

"If it weren't for representing Hong Kong this time, Mr. Li probably wouldn't have come to Shanghai, right?" I asked.

"I wouldn't dare say that I'm representing, but this time it's a rare opportunity to visit friends I haven't seen for many years, and also to take this opportunity to reunite with football fans in Shanghai."

"After going to Hong Kong, are you still as interested in football as you were in Shanghai?"

"Of course. A person who has a special love for something is unwilling to give up that love from beginning to end, let alone that I have been 'inseparable' from football since I was a child!"

"Yes, that's why you deserve to be called the 'Football Freak'!" I said, looking at him with a smile. "So, you've been playing football since you were a child until now. I believe you must have a lot of insights that ordinary football players can't comprehend, right?"

"That's not necessarily true." He quickly took my words and said, "Playing football is just like doing any other career. You have to 'persevere' to make progress, because this kind of thing can't be learned to the point of perfection in a day or two. I dare not exaggerate how good my football skills are, but it is true that I have suffered for it for many years. I remember when I was studying in elementary school, I was only that tall, but I loved football so much that I didn't even want to eat sometimes, and I would compete with others at every turn, wishing I could sleep on the football field all day long. Later, because many children didn't have my kind of fanaticism and were unwilling to work as hard as I did without end, the number of people who played football with me sometimes decreased, and even the situation where I didn't have an opponent became commonplace. But my passion for playing football didn't decrease because of this. On the contrary, maybe I played even more vigorously alone, because the best thing about playing football alone is that no one is stealing the ball, and the ball can always be kicked on my own feet." As he said this, he couldn't help but laugh.

"When a person plays football alone, I think it must be very strenuous, right?"

"No, it's not strenuous at all. When there's no one to play against me, I kick the ball against the wall, kicking it back and forth like playing 'Jai Alai', and then kicking it again, over and over again, until I'm sweating and my head feels sore. In this way, it wasn't until the ninth year of the Republic of China that I switched to playing with a big ball. At that time, I was confident that I had a good grasp of football, so the way I practiced was more skillful and practical than before."

"Some people say that you only know how to use your right foot to kick the ball, and your left foot can only help the use of your right foot, and you can't shoot with it, is that right?"

"That's not true. Generally speaking, people use their right foot more to kick the ball, and it's not that there aren't people who can't kick with their left foot, but that's all because they're too casual and not elegant enough. Although they use their right foot more often, it also depends on how the ball is coming. I've been practicing using both feet equally since I was a child. However, when I first started kicking, my left foot was indeed a little less flexible than my right foot, and sometimes when the ball came to my foot, I wanted to use my left foot, but my right foot just wouldn't listen to orders and went forward. Later, I came up with a method, which was not to wear a shoe on my right foot. If it wanted to go forward, I would feel a lightness on my toe and remember to use my left foot. I kicked like this for a long time, and gradually I got used to being able to use both feet at the same time. If someone says that I only know how to use my right foot, it's probably because they saw me kick 'penalty kicks'; because it's impossible not to use your right foot for 'twelve-yard kicks'!"

"That's right, I've seen you use your right foot most of the time when you kick 'penalty kicks'. Maybe your right foot is more reliable, isn't it that every time you kick a 'penalty kick', it goes in?" I said jokingly.

"It's not that my foot is reliable," he said seriously. "It's useless to just kick well, because the goalkeeper isn't dead. You also have to use some wit in your mind at the time. For example, if the goalkeeper is standing on the right, but his defense is on the left, because he expects you to take advantage of the gap to attack, but if you go the other way and shoot towards the side he's standing on, he will definitely only see your foot move and run to the left, but he doesn't expect that your ball will just take advantage of the emptiness on his right side and drive straight in. By the time he turns around to save it, it's already 'too late'. You have to use wit to kick the ball, there's no mistake about that. That's why many people misunderstand that I don't want to run when I play, and say that I'm kicking a 'lazy ball', because they don't understand the role my mind is playing at the time."

"It's true that you don't run when you kick the ball, but in fact, there's no way for you to run at the time."

"That's right! Every time I play against someone, because I have a little bit of fame, as soon as I walk onto the field, I get 'watched', and there's no way for me to run. But I don't think it's very useful to rely solely on running to kick the ball. The most important thing is to be able to see the rising and falling points of a ball. Usually, when you play against someone, you must never just look up at the ball and run after it in the field. That's a stupid move that wastes energy and doesn't get you the ball. The best thing to do is to predict where it will fall when the ball rises, and then quickly run to that side to wait. This way, you can avoid the enemy's attention, and your feet will have enough energy to catch and kick the ball that is about to arrive. Every time I play against foreigners, people don't see me running all over the field to catch the ball, but when the ball gets to my feet, it's not easily taken away by others."

"Needless to say, the Hong Kong team can probably win the football championship in this National Games, right?"

"That's hard to say!"

"In your opinion, which team is more hopeful?"

"Probably!" He lowered his head and pondered for a while: "I think it won't be outside these four teams: Hong Kong, East China, Central China, and Malaya!"

"Does the Malayan team play well?"

"Yes, that's right. The talents of this team are almost all top players gathered from Singapore, Penang, and Java, so they are more confident when they play. Secondly, the talents of East China and South China are also some veterans who have been on the battlefield for a long time, and their strengths are still average. It's not easy to predict who will win when they clash in the future. As for the Hong Kong team, of course they are not weak, but they haven't had the opportunity to scrimmage with other friendly teams yet, so I don't dare to be confident."

"As for the teams from North China and Central China, I'm afraid there's not much hope, right?"

"Individually, the talents of North China are not bad, but as a whole team, it seems that they lack training in communication. Central China is of course inferior! In summary, it's not that their talents are not as good as those of East China, South China, or Hong Kong, but because of environmental reasons, they rarely have the opportunity to compete and practice with good teams, so it's difficult to improve their level of skill. As for the teams from South China, Hong Kong, and East China, they have good opportunities to compete with foreign teams often, so their skills naturally improve easily. However, the Shanghai football scene has only deteriorated in recent years compared to previous years."

"It is said that you are participating in the National Games this time not only in football, but also in tennis. Did you start practicing tennis after going to Hong Kong?"

"No, I started learning tennis in Australia in the sixteenth year of the Republic of China." As he said this, he took out a pocket watch from his pocket and looked at it, then continued, "I remember it was after attending the Far Eastern Games held in Japan that a group of us went on a distant expedition to Australia, where we met Lin Baohua, and my desire to learn tennis started burning. After returning to China, I was deeply guided by Lin Baohua, Qiu Feihai, and others, and after exchanging ideas with Jiang Daozhang and Zheng Zhaojia, my interest in tennis became more and more intense, and I practiced every day without end. By the nineteenth year of the Republic of China, Lao Jiang and I partnered to win the Shanghai Open Hard Court Doubles Championship, which confirmed the possibility of tennis continuing to be linked to me. But when I went south to Hong Kong that year, my tennis still couldn't attract much attention. It wasn't until the last Hong Kong Open that I defeated the four-year runner-up 'Finch' in one battle, and then after another battle, I won several times against the defending champion 'Lin Zhen', which made people surprised at how quickly my skills had improved. Therefore, the eyes of the selection committee for inter-port competitions were cast on me."

"Can you also make a prediction about the tennis championship in the National Games?"

"Needless to say! The championship this time is of course in the bag for the Shanghai team. The Shanghai team has superior talents, and the Hong Kong team is certainly not their 'match'. I only hope to lose as few 'eggs' as possible in the competition, that's our blessing!" He couldn't help but laugh out loud.

As we were talking about this, he seemed to remember something again, took out his watch and looked at it again, and his demeanor was not as relaxed as before, so I quickly got up to say goodbye and came out.

Special Article

Observations on the United States' Silver Purchase Policy 207

— Lin Baozhong

Since Roosevelt stepped onto the American political stage as President, he has come up with various remedies for the decline of his country's industry, the surge in unemployed workers, and the economic downturn in society. Among them, the silver purchase policy has won the sympathy of the whole country. The nature of this policy and its impact on China's economy are discussed in order below:

(I) Contents of the Silver Policy.

The main points of this policy are: (A) The ratio of silver to gold should be increased to one-quarter of its currency reserves. In other words, the ratio of silver reserves to gold reserves should be one to three. (B) The U.S. Treasury Department may purchase silver from abroad at any time. The degree of silver purchase is until the silver reserves are equal to one-quarter of the metallic currency reserves. Its price (1) must not exceed its price as currency, (2) for all silver that was already in the United States on May 1, 1934, the purchase price must not exceed 50 cents per ounce in U.S. dollars. In other words, silver outside the United States or silver transported into the United States after May 1 may be purchased at a price above 50 cents. (C) If the price of silver exceeds the price of its silver coins, or the total value of silver coin reserves is greater than 25% of the total value of gold and silver reserves used for currency, the Secretary of the Treasury may sell silver at any time. In addition, the Secretary of the Treasury is also allowed to issue silver certificates, the face value of which must not be lower than the cost of the silver purchased, and the Secretary of the Treasury is authorized to manage, investigate, or prohibit the purchase, import, and transshipment of silver, and to promulgate such regulations as he deems necessary to implement this plan.

If the silver purchase plan is implemented seriously, then according to the United States' recent reserves of approximately US$7,776,000,000, one-third of which is US$2,589,000,000, this is the value of the amount of silver required for the silver purchase plan. Currently, there are only silver coins worth $841,000,000 in U.S. currency, so an additional $1,74 ,000,000,000 in gold is needed to reach the one-quarter ratio. The current price of silver used for currency in the United States is US$1.29 per ounce, so the amount of U.S. dollars in silver is 1,355,000,000 ounces, which is also the amount of silver the United States intends to buy. This amount of silver, calculated at a market price of no more than 50 cents per ounce in U.S. dollars, requires approximately US$677,500,000.

(II) Sources of silver to be purchased by the United States

There are approximately the following sources of silver to be purchased by the United States: (A) The current excess supply of silver worldwide, that is, in the hands of speculators, is approximately 16,300,000 ounces. In theory, this silver should be the first to be sold. (B) Last year's silver production was 160,000,000 ounces, and this year it has not been able to increase significantly (because silver is mostly a by-product of other minerals, and the production volume is not easy to increase in a short time), so assuming it to be 180,000,000 ounces, it is also possible for the U.S. government to absorb most of it. (C) According to the Pittman International Silver Agreement, the Indian government can sell 35,000,000 ounces each year for the next four years. (D) The maximum estimated silver reserves in Shanghai are approximately 600,000,000 ounces, of which 260,000,000 ounces are owned by foreign banks and 340,000,000 ounces are owned by Chinese banks.

In addition to these four sources, Spain and Russia may also sell silver, but the quantity is very small. However, based on the examination of these four major sources, if the United States only relies on the first and second sources, then by the end of the year, it will only be able to obtain 320,000,000 ounces, which is far from the amount it wants to purchase. However, in fact, all silver owners want to wait for a good price to sell, and China and India have no reason not to sell silver to the U.S. government unless the government finds a way to prevent it. Therefore, if the United States is determined to buy silver, it will undoubtedly buy silver from China and India, especially China, where the degree of silver sales is stronger than in any other country. Because China is a silver-based country, speculators are generally afraid of the export ban on silver, and will try their best to transport it out for sale. Moreover, it is more cost-effective to offset China's annual trade deficit with silver. Foreign banks in the past imported silver at extremely low costs, and now they have a high price to sell, so what is there to be unwilling to do? Currently, silver exports have reached more than 30 million ounces according to customs statistics, and are still

Page 21

Continuing to be shipped out for export, because foreign banks have recognized that the transshipment of silver is a very good investment, they will naturally ship it out in a steady stream.

(III) Motives of the U.S. Government in Implementing This Policy

As for the motives of the U.S. government in implementing the silver purchase policy, according to general observations, there are approximately two points: (A) To offset more dangerous bills. Since the current U.S. Congress convened, the silver faction's congressmen have exaggerated their proposals to the extreme, and even bills of sixteen to one or even fifteen to one almost passed, so the silver faction has the authority to manipulate Congress. Although the U.S. President found it difficult to endorse such bills, he had to find a way to perfunctorily approve a more flexible silver purchase bill in order to win the favor of the silver faction's congressmen, and its purpose was certainly not to greatly increase silver transport. This observation is the argument of people in the general foreign exchange market, who believe that the silver purchase bill has the same effect as the previous Thomas Amendment and the 1934 Gold Reserve Act, and that its purpose is political, not monetary, to adopt this consistent policy. (B) To promote price increases or prevent price declines. The silver purchase bill has the same nature as the previous gold purchase plan. If implemented in accordance with the law, it would be sufficient to help raise prices. The gold purchase plan was about suppressing the price of the U.S. currency, thereby raising prices expressed in U.S. currency, but in fact, the price increase was not as fast as the gold price increase, so the gold purchase plan failed. As for this time's purchase of silver and issuance of silver certificates, although it can increase currency and raise prices, it is difficult to predict whether raising prices will be as effective as expected. However, if U.S. prices cannot rise upward in the afternoon of this year, or even have a tendency to fall downward, Roosevelt may also use this policy to alleviate the emergency in order to save prices. Therefore, the motive for implementing this policy may also be to prevent the decline in prices.

Currently, the changes in the U.S. economy have been much calmer than before, labor unrest has gradually decreased, and industries and businesses have gradually become more active with the silver certificates from the government. Most of the unemployed workers have also found a considerable solution to their panic. However, our country has suffered greatly from it. Domestic silver prices have risen with the trend, and silver has flowed to the United States involuntarily. As a result, prices have continued to fall rapidly, and industries and businesses were already in a very depressed state. Coupled with the United States' increase in the purchasing power of the general public, they have collapsed and collapsed one after another. The impact on the rural economy has been even more profound, and the rural by-products can be said to be completely destroyed. If this situation continues, China's future will be unimaginable!

Miscellaneous Works

Arrogance 208

— Yucai

My grandfather, when he was alive, was extremely fond of me, his fatherless grandson. He toiled his entire life, and in his later years, he placed almost all of his hopes on me. I sometimes felt that I was the only one in the family who resembled my grandfather. I had the same stubborn temper as him, and I was confident that I would one day accomplish the same kind of things he had.

My grandfather bore the heavy burden of providing for the food and clothing of over a dozen people spanning three generations, so until his very last breath, he was like a heavily laden camel, even though he was already very old. He spent the entire year managing his business in the city. Three or four times a year, he would return home from the city with his hunched back and gray hair for a short rest.

The month or so that my grandfather was at home was the liveliest time for our family. He would bring back fruits from the city like apples, grapes, and crabapples, distributing them one by one to us children. We would hold the stems of the apples and run around the streets, showing them off. Once, he even brought back a small toy gun. After dinner, when the old man was in high spirits after drinking some wine, he would squint his eyes happily, pretending to aim the gun and shoot us. We would grab my grandfather's hand and laugh wildly, and my grandfather would be so happy that tears would stream down his face.

Our neighbor, an elderly Mrs. Li, was already in her nineties. She was a generation older than my grandfather. Besides being slightly hard of hearing, she was still quite spry. She often visited the neighbors, especially our house, almost every day, to chat for a few words. This had become almost a daily routine. When my grandfather was home, he would happily drink about half a kilogram of Shaoxing wine with each meal, talking to us children. Mrs. Li would come to do her routine at this time. Seeing my grandfather drinking Shaoxing wine, she would sit down next to him. My grandfather knew that she didn't like to drink, so he would pick out some soft, easy-to-eat foods for her to taste and loudly tell her the names of those rare foods. We children watched Mrs. Li nodding her head in such a way, and everyone laughed heartily again. Seeing the children's happy smiles, Mrs. Li patted my grandfather's back and said, "Zhiqing, you are really blessed with good fortune. You have such a harmonious pair of grandsons who will be even better than you in the future!" My grandfather had nothing to say. He stroked his beard slightly, a mixture of bitterness and joy welling up in his heart. Finally, he let out a long sigh.

My grandfather loved to hear such compliments, and he also loved that moment of bittersweet flavor. He had indeed placed all his hopes on me.

Later, with my grandfather's fervent hopes, I entered normal school. Three years of cruel education completely wounded my childlike innocence. My personality suddenly changed from innocent purity to cold melancholy. These years were truly the most unfortunate years of my life, harming my vitality. In June, I dragged my sorrowful body back to my hometown, my heart forever filled with gloom. Every day, I wanted to emulate the poets and use pure wine to wash away the sorrows in my heart. Sometimes, I would hide alone in a deserted place, holding a book of Tang poetry and reciting it aloud. When I read a passage that evoked a bleak scene, I felt as if I were actually in that situation, and unconsciously, hot tears would fill my cheeks. In this way, it was as if I had hysteria! After a few days, my grandfather returned home for his summer rest as usual, but my heart was no longer as innocent as it had been when I was a child. My grandfather was not very happy when he saw my state this time.

One afternoon, my mother told me that my grandfather had quietly returned to the city. This made me feel very abrupt. My mother also told me, "Your grandfather left very unhappy. He said, 'Yun'er is very arrogant. This child has no great hope.' The old man seemed very angry and dejected!"

Hearing my mother's words, my melancholy heart became even more melancholy. I thought about why my elderly grandfather had returned to the city so quietly, and I thought about how my gray-haired grandfather was being tormented by pain because of me, gnawing at his heart that had been wounded so many times! The more I thought about it, the more I finally cried!

I had disappointed even my most loving grandfather!

Arrogant. That is how my grandfather criticized me, and that is how he disliked me. Those so-called teachers had also criticized me in this way, but I remained arrogant forever. I had just left childhood when arrogance occupied my entire life.

In the following years, my grandfather passed away, and the family suffered repeated misfortunes. The burden that my grandfather had carried for decades unconditionally fell on my shoulders, but I still had that same arrogant temper.

"Yun'er is very arrogant. This child has no great hope!" My grandfather's words often echoed in my mind. I constantly savored the sad expression on my grandfather's face when he said these words.

I have been drifting in the sea of humanity for several years now. During these years, I have suffered so many cold stares from the world, so much cruel bullying. I am often angry, but I often endure it. I swallow the tears that fill my eyes because I still have to bear that heavy burden!

I have cured my arrogance. I have cured the problem that my grandfather could not cure. I am no longer arrogant. I endure all the sufferings of the world, bearing a heavy burden of life like my grandfather did when he was alive, treading the long road of life to the end!

Grandfather! Your Yun'er is no longer arrogant, but where is this child's hope now?

Sunday Literary Society

Idealistic Literary Criticism 209

— Xingcong

In philosophy, there is the opposition between idealism and materialism. Similarly, in literary criticism, there is the opposition between idealistic criticism and sociological scientific criticism. Moreover, in the field of literary criticism, idealism has always had a great influence. Horizontally speaking, so-called appreciation criticism, aesthetic criticism, impressionistic criticism, and ethical criticism, although each has its own characteristics, can all be said to belong to the ranks of idealistic literary criticism in the end. Vertically speaking, from the literary criticism of Plato and Aristotle in ancient times, through the Middle Ages, through the Renaissance, and then through Classicism and Romanticism, all literary criticism before Naturalism can be said to be idealistic criticism. In other words, all literary criticism before Taine was dominated by idealistic theories.

In fact, Plato explained poetry with illusory inspiration. He paid special attention to ethical effects, so he argued that "the function of the poet, the privilege of the poet, and the reason for the poet's existence is to provide us with non-realistic things." His literary criticism, guided by such a view, was naturally very mysterious. When he was dissatisfied with poets, he even banished them from his "Republic," believing that "poets are blasphemers of God." At the same time, although Aristotle is regarded as the "father of literary criticism," and his "Poetics" is indeed the most valuable literary criticism work of ancient times that no one can deny, due to the limitations of the times, from a modern perspective, we cannot help but say that even his famous "Poetics" is not a perfect work. Moreover, in the end, his masterpiece is still biased towards pure technical research and is written from an idealistic standpoint. In "Poetics," Aristotle attempted to explain the origin of poetry with the instinct of imitation and the instinct of harmonious desire, which led him to enter the world of idealism. Furthermore, he discussed narrative poetry, tragedy, comedy, and Greek hymns from an idealistic perspective. For example, in commenting on tragedy, he made the following claims about the characters' personalities: (1) The character should be good; (2) The character should have appropriateness, such as a man being brave is very good, but a woman being brave is not good-looking; (3) The character should be faithful to life; (4) The character should be consistent from beginning to end. From this, it can be seen that he did not objectively explain why the characters appearing in the plays are like that and what their meaning is from a social perspective, but rather subjectively stipulated how the characters' personalities should be. Due to his subjective idealistic viewpoint, in his principles of literary criticism, like Plato, he also paid attention to ethical effects. Moreover, he also made many rules to be followed in form, such as the well-known "three unities" of Classicism after the Renaissance, which came from his "Poetics."

During the Middle Ages, because mankind was dominated by a natural economy, they developed extremely isolated and helpless thoughts and feelings. Everything could only hope for the help of heaven and the spirit. Therefore, the expression of various human thoughts at this time was stained with a strong theological color, and various literary works naturally expressed mystical thoughts and feelings. Such as the so-called heroic poems, religious moral poems, knight stories, parables in the Bible, and Oriental tales and legends, are all painted with the colors of miracles and mystery. As for literary criticism, it was naturally theological. By the time of the Renaissance, although this medieval theological thought had ended, with the revival of the spirit of antiquity, Aristotle's idealistic literary criticism showed its new development again. The so-called classical literary criticism can be said to be the revival and development of Aristotle's literary criticism. Later, the rise of Romanticism, although it broke the "three unities" of Classicism, liberated emotions, and developed individuality, also because of this, Romantic literary criticism was also dressed in the colorful clothes of idealism. Like literary propositions, Wordsworth's literary criticism, are all idealistic.

From the above description, we can see that from Plato and Aristotle to the Romantic era, literary criticism was dressed in the colorful clothes of idealism. Although in the middle of this, the literary criticism that appeared in each era was a reflection of the thoughts of the social people of each era, and because the social people of each era were different, the literary criticism of each era also had its own characteristics. But in the end, we can still assert that the literary criticism from ancient times to the Romantic era was dressed in the colorful clothes of idealism. For example, Classicism and Romanticism, from the perspective of the development of literary history, the latter is the negation of the former, and their ideas are certainly different. But in that they both subjectively advocated that literature should be like this and did not evaluate literature from an objective social perspective, in that they used "reason" or "emotion" to explain literature and could not further examine the source of the thoughts and feelings expressed in literary works and their social value, we can still say that their literary criticism is also idealistic criticism.

Of course, idealistic literary criticism did not disappear after Romanticism. On the contrary, it continued to appear in various forms in the literary criticism world. However, we do not want to elaborate on this here. What is most important to us at this time is to explain and criticize several major modern idealistic literary criticism.

Speaking of idealism, people will never forget Hegel. He is not only the completer of the idealistic philosophical system, the greatest representative of idealistic philosophy, but also the representative of the greatest idealistic view of art in modern times. His famous "Aesthetics" can be said to be a classic of idealistic aesthetics. In the middle of this, he has a very detailed analysis of many artistic finished products, but in the end, he always explains art with empty spirit, ideas, and inspiration. For example, although his explanation of medieval Gothic architecture is very detailed, he fundamentally believes that all the characteristics of Gothic architecture are expressions of the Christian spirit. As for why Gothic temples express the Christian spirit rather than other spirits? How did the so-called Christian spirit of the Middle Ages arise? Hegel did not consider this fundamental question.

In addition to Hegel, Schopenhauer is also a famous idealist; and he has also published more mysterious discussions on art and literature. He fundamentally denies that art and literature are products of human society. He once said that even if the universe loses its existence, music still exists, as long as there is wind. As for literary criticism, he mystified criticism because of his worship of genius. He said at the beginning of his discussion of criticism: "The following brief notes on critical talent are mostly to show that the world does not have this thing. It is a very rare bird, in fact, almost as rare as the phoenix that comes out once every five hundred years." Since he believed that criticism was so mysterious, his own criticism of literature would naturally be very mysterious. In addition to mysteriously praising the talents of many geniuses and sighing at their experiences, the result was almost to eliminate literary criticism.

The development of idealistic literary criticism reached its extreme in Aestheticism. The literary criticism of Wilde, the first of Aestheticism, is its representative. In Wilde's view, nothing has any meaning except for empty, mysterious "rarity," "charm," and "beauty." He once used his aesthetic theory to criticize Zola, saying: "From an artistic point of view, Zola's works are almost worthless, only zero points. The characters in his works are all decadent and pitiful people, the crystallization of sin. The lives of these characters are meaningless records. Who can pay attention to these people? Our requirements for art are rarity, charm, and imagination, simply beauty." This is really the expression of the extreme development of the mysterious theory of idealism. Under such a mysterious theory, Zola, the naturalist who pays attention to "sketching from life," is of course to be negated.

However, after Wilde's aesthetic literary criticism, idealistic literary criticism continued to appear in various forms in the critical world. Here we can cite the currently popular impressionistic criticism. The so-called impressionistic criticism denies a certain standard of literary criticism and evaluates literature solely based on personal subjective temporary impressions. Impressionists hold a personal subjective skeptical attitude, do not believe in the existence of objective literary criticism standards, and fundamentally deny that literature has a practical social basis. The famous impressionist A. France said in his "Literary Life": "Aesthetics has no solid foundation, it is a castle in the air. Some people want to place its foundation on ethics, but there is no so-called ethics. Sociology also does not have it. ... To establish criticism, people often say tradition and common acceptance. However, these things do not exist. General public opinion recognizes a certain work, this is a fact. However, this is preconceived, it is definitely not from a free state of mind, nor is it the result of spontaneous love. The works that everyone praises are works that no one has ever savored." In this way, everything is gone, and what remains is only the individual's subjective impression, then the so-called individual's subjective impression is without practical basis, mysterious and incomprehensible. The influence of such mysterious and incomprehensible impressionism even makes people fundamentally deny the existence of objective truth, saying that there is no correct literary theory at all, and even saying that there is no such thing as an introduction to literature. But in the end, its theory is still a theoretical form of idealism existing in objective society.

The French Wan Long said,"No science has been oppressed by metaphysical fantasies as much as aesthetics. Since Plato until modern public doctrine, the general public often makes art into a delicate fantasy and mysterious object, so that the highest words are actually restricted to the special scope of beautiful, unchanging, God's scope, substantial ideas." This is a correct diagnosis. Because art and literature are the uppermost social ideologies that are farther away from the social foundation, and it is not easy to directly see the relationship between them and the social foundation, so metaphysics - idealism is the easiest to extend its power in this field in various poses.

Special Description

Overseas Chinese in the World (X) (3) 210

— Zhong Minyi

New Zealand

New Zealand, also commonly known as New Zealand, is also one of the five major self-governing dominions of Great Britain. The status of overseas Chinese here is roughly the same as in Australia. According to investigations, more than fifty years ago, there were 4,215 overseas Chinese here. However, the local government and people paid very close attention to overseas Chinese and frequently ostracized them. In 1907, the new government stipulated that all overseas Chinese entering the country must pass an English test of one hundred words. As a result, overseas Chinese in New Zealand could not develop.

Most of the overseas Chinese in New Zealand are from Guangdong, and most of them are small businessmen and horticulturalists. It is said that their lives are not very bad.

The West Indies are originally the world of black people, but the political and economic power is entirely in the hands of Europeans and Americans. Because overseas Chinese are able to endure hardship and are hard-working, they also have quite a bit of strength in general industry and commerce; although recently the mixed race of black people and white people here have been quite active in general occupational sectors and are competing with overseas Chinese, they cannot shake their inherent position.

Later, Ya Mengquan came up with an idea to flatten the uneven icebergs, so everyone worked together and in twenty-four days, they built an airfield 500 meters long. The six people safely returned on a plane.

After this failure, Ya Mengquan felt that the plane was not suitable for Arctic exploration. He had failed with steamships before, so he thought of huge airships and later borrowed one from Italy. This time, seventeen people went, and although they encountered danger when they were about to reach their destination, they eventually succeeded. After more than thirty years of hard work, Ya Mengquan achieved his life's wish. (End)

Since Wu Bangfan joined Yihua to oversee business matters, Yihua's business has been thriving daily.

Experimental Theater Troupe Will Perform Soon 216

Plays: Good and Evil, The Fugitive, The Last Prayer

Since the Experimental Theater Troupe participated in the first performance of the French Molière play The Miser at the Flood Relief Fundraising Association, it has completely separated from the Performing Arts Laboratory. Currently, Liu Yawei and Chen Tu, former members of the Chunqiu Society, are responsible for promoting the work of the troupe. Yesterday, a performance committee was established at Xinya, and it was decided to realize the second performance before the end of October. The selected plays are Good and Evil (three-act play), The Last Prayer (two-act play), and The Fugitive (one-act play). It is said that in addition to Liu Yawei, Lu Shi and Zuo Ming and other playwrights will also help with directing.
